Citizens on Nanjing Road Petitioned the Municipal Government Yesterday 99

Regarding the Telephone Price Increase

Wang Lianfang, Chairman of the Nanjing Road Business Federation, and Ji Jiannan and Sun Wenyi, Standing Committee Members of the Citizens' District Branch, went to see the Mayor yesterday on behalf of the two associations, carrying a written petition (transcribed below) to oppose the telephone price increase. Secretary-General Yu Hongjun received them and the three representatives stated their intentions and delivered the official document. Secretary-General Yu accepted the request and promised to immediately send a letter to the First Special District Bureau of Works to order the Shanghai Telephone Company to stop disconnecting lines and to restore the lines that have already been disconnected. The representatives were satisfied and left. The attached petition is as follows: One Petition Regarding the Increasingly Perverse Actions of the Shanghai Telephone Company and the Continuous Disconnection of Lines, Requesting Serious Protest and Prompt Correction of the Price Increase. We, the undersigned, hereby petition the government regarding the illegal price increase and the rash suspension of telephone service by the Shanghai Telephone Company. We have repeatedly petitioned your government to correct this and to stop the company, but the Shanghai Telephone Company, relying on the approval of the Bureau of Works, has become increasingly perverse, continuing to disconnect lines relentlessly. The people are outraged and the situation is escalating. The Bureau of Works only uses the company's one-sided interests as the absolute reason for the price increase and published an article in the newspapers on November 18 defending the company, without stopping the company from continuing to use illegal means. The Bureau of Works sees the approval of the price increase as its supreme power, compounding errors and acting arbitrarily. Although the citizens and various public organizations have made various statements and repeatedly appealed, the Bureau of Works has turned a deaf ear, allowing the citizens to be slaughtered. The citizens are unwilling to submit and have come to the association to request a transfer of their petition. We have long admired your care for the people and your understanding of the difficulties of merchants. We cannot remain silent about the suffering of the citizens in the special district. We have no choice but to send three committee members, Wang Lianfang, Ji Jiannan, and Sun Wenyi, to visit you and convey the feelings of the people. We humbly request that you grant us an audience, give us instructions, and promptly lodge a serious protest and correct the situation according to law to ensure social stability and quell public anger.

Order Received by the Municipal Government

Planning to Dredge Lu Jingpu, Pu Hui Tang, and Other Waterways 106

The Shanghai-Songhu War Zone Rehabilitation Committee previously suggested to the Executive Yuan that the rivers and harbors in the Shanghai-Songhu area should be dredged. The suggestion stated that the rivers and harbors in the Shanghai-Songhu area are branched and originate from the Huangpu River. Vessels enter and exit with the tides. Over the years, they have become silted up. The accumulation has become so high and compounded by the effluent from factories and residents polluting the waterways. Near the city, the stench is unbearable; in the countryside, drinking water is scarce. If immediate repairs are not made, there is a risk of complete blockage. Due to limited financial resources, it is necessary to selectively dredge key waterways. Besides the section of the Dachang-Miaohang Jianbangpu, which is the shallowest, the most important tributaries are the Lu Jingpu and Shenjin Port in Zhabei, and the Puhui Tang and Rihui Port in West Shanghai. These waterways connect to the concessions and are vital to the area's appearance. Dredging Lu Jingpu should be connected to the Taoxi Sitang to reach Yunzao Creek, so that the river system is fully connected. Dredging Puhui Tang should include filling in Zhaojiabang to eliminate the source of factory wastewater. The cost of the two river projects is estimated at 200,000 yuan, to be allocated by the committee. The task of filling in the waterway should be assigned to the Shanghai Municipal Government, as the filled land can be sold to cover the cost of digging ditches and transporting earth. The Executive Yuan deemed the committee's proposal feasible and ordered the Shanghai Municipal Government and Jiangsu Provincial Government to assist in its implementation. The Municipal Government has also received orders to instruct the Public Works Bureau to comply.

Biography of Chuan Xiao'an's Trip to Wuhan 109

▲Attending the Opening Ceremony of the Bank of Communications Branch ▲Touring the Scenic Spots of the Three Towns of Wuhan Since returning to Shanghai from Dalian last year, Mr. Chuan Xiao'an has stayed at home, avoiding public life. In mid-July, he suddenly traveled west to Hankou, causing much speculation. When someone interviewed Mr. Chuan at Jinhuisitang yesterday, he replied that his trip to Hankou was to attend the opening ceremony of the Bank of Communications Hankou branch and to tour the scenic spots of the Three Towns of Wuhan. While in Wuhan, he visited General Chiang Kai-shek at the Yihua Village residence for a forty-minute conversation. The discussion focused on the commercial situation and market conditions in Nanjing, Shanghai, and Wuhan. Chiang Kai-shek believes that the establishment of Bank of Communications branches in Nanjing and Hankou will promote market prosperity and benefit industry and commerce, and he expressed his appreciation and awarded the Hankou branch the plaque “[Utilizing Resources for the Benefit of the People]” and the Nanjing branch the plaque “[Economic Pioneering],” demonstrating his dedication to promoting industry and commerce. He added that the market in Wuhan is gradually recovering, and the atmosphere is quite vibrant.

Shipping Industry

Petition to Exempt Ship Tickets from Stamp Tax 113

▲Representatives Sent to Petition the Stamp Tax Bureau Yesterday ▲Submitting a Request to the Ministry of Finance to Order the Bureau to Cancel the Stamp Tax Jiangsu Stamp Tax Branch Bureau Chief Xu Zhicheng, under orders, is handling the addition of stamp tax to steamship passenger tickets. The Bureau announced to all ticket agencies that starting December 1st, all steamship passenger tickets must have stamps affixed. As most of the steamship tickets sold are for foreign companies, enforcement is bound to cause difficulties. They jointly requested the Ministry of Finance for exemption. Yesterday, the Ticket Industry Association and the China Shipping Mutual Aid Association held a meeting to discuss a joint request to the Jiangsu Stamp Tax Bureau. The details are as follows:

▲Six Articles of Ship Ticket Stamp Regulations The six articles of ship ticket stamp regulations are as follows: 1. Various accounting books used on ships must have stamps affixed at a value of 1 jiao. 2. Steamship passenger tickets priced at less than 1 yuan must have a stamp affixed at a value of 1 fen, and those priced over 1 yuan must have a stamp affixed at a value of 2 fen, with the value increasing accordingly. 3. Steamship ticket offices and travel agencies that sell steamship tickets must affix stamps in accordance with the regulations. 4. When affixing a stamp, the stamp must be stamped with a seal or signature at the designated location. 5. Stamps that have been affixed must not be removed and reused. 6. There are five types of stamps: 1 fen (blue), 2 fen (yellow), 1 jiao (red), 5 jiao (purple), and 1 yuan (blue). All are stamped with the words "Jiangsu Shanghai South District." Steamship tickets will also have a special "Steamship Ticket Only" stamp to distinguish them.

▲Representatives Petition The China Shipping Mutual Aid Association and the Ticket Industry Association believe that steamship ticket stamps for foreign steamships present a particular difficulty. They held a second meeting yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM to discuss the matter. In addition to deciding to petition the Ministry of Finance for exemption, they also dispatched representatives Zhu Ruiqing and Wang Bingquan (Mutual Aid Association) and Wu Zhaochu and Liu Hanguang (Ticket Industry Association) to the Shanghai Stamp Tax Bureau to petition. The four representatives arrived at the Bureau at 4:00 PM. Secretary Zhu of the Bureau received them and stated that he would relay their request to the Director, asking that the implementation of steamship ticket stamps be temporarily suspended until the Ministry of Finance has issued a response, and that inspectors not be dispatched to avoid misunderstandings. The representatives then departed, feeling that the outcome was satisfactory.

▲Letter to the Ministry of Finance The China Shipping Mutual Aid Association and the Ticket Industry Association yesterday sent a letter to the Ministry of Finance, stating: "Regarding the request to exempt steamship passenger tickets from stamp tax in order to alleviate commercial difficulties and maintain the shipping industry, we respectfully request your review and approval. According to a report from the business directors of various steamships that are members of this association: "According to a notice from the Jiangsu Stamp Tax Branch Bureau (omitted), six articles of stamp regulations are attached. We believe that the stamp tax is a national tax and should be complied with. However, last year we suffered from floods, and this year we have been affected by war. Commerce has been severely damaged. Ordinary passengers are unable to pay the ticket price, let alone the additional stamp tax. In addition, foreign companies have not been required to affix stamps to steamship tickets for decades, and to implement this suddenly is bound to cause difficulties and be rejected." Therefore, we respectfully submit this letter and request that it be forwarded to the Ministry of Finance, requesting exemption in order to maintain the shipping industry." The above-mentioned statement from the business directors is true and reflects the difficulties in affixing stamps to steamship passenger tickets. Therefore, we respectfully submit this letter and request that you consider the difficulties faced by merchants and grant exemption from stamp tax for steamship passenger tickets in order to maintain the shipping industry. [Anxious and waiting for orders], we respectfully submit this letter to Finance Minister Song Ziwen.

Appeal to Waive Business Tax 114

▲If One Moves All Will Perish The Native Cloth Industry Association of Shanghai sent letters to the National Government and the Ministries of Finance and Industry yesterday, requesting that the collection of business tax on native cloth be stopped. "[On behalf of the request, instruct the Fujian, Zhejiang, and Jiangsu Provincial Finance Departments to investigate and order the business tax collectors to exempt native cloth from business tax in order to create a precedent." The National Manual Native Cloth Business Tax Exemption case was mainly initiated by the Association, who expressed that the poor people suffered. The case was compiled and submitted to the Legislative Yuan for review. Zou Guofu's decision was that in December of the 20th year, all provinces and cities received instructions from the Executive Yuan one after another that native cloth business tax should be exempt. What happened was that the business tax collectors in the second district of Zhejiang Province, in disregard of the established case and the order of the ministry, and without regard to the people's difficulties, added business tax. With the administrative orders in hand, the tax collectors did not care about it. The Zhejiang Association has already telegraphed to the Zhejiang provincial authorities, requesting a halt. It was reported to the industry by Chongming and Qidong counties in Jiangsu that the business tax collectors there had already followed suit and forced the payment of taxes by police force. In the Fujian province report, Ninde Sanbu and other places have also had the intent to re-impose native cloth tax and impose harsh taxes. The association has asked and stated. The case of all provinces and cities is not requested to be halted, and the business tax collector of the provincial district makes inappropriate remarks and harasses the lives of the people. Since manual hand-woven native cloth was made tax-free, Fang Qi Chaoye Shang, the next teacher's code of practice, published clothes to save the country, and made a grand wish to strengthen the country and expand people's livelihoods. The two provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang are native cloth producing areas, and the three northeastern provinces are the most prosperous selling areas, followed by Min and Guangdong. Since the Japanese army invaded Liaoning on September 18, the goods from the three provinces have been transported for a long time and have been suspended. In the battle zone, houses were destroyed, equipment was lost, and local sages did their best to request assistance from the government and all walks of life. It is not the time to solve the difficulties by building and setting up equipment and lending capital. The people in the war-affected leased area have suffered a lot. The merchants are in distress, and everyone knows that. The business tax officers are growing up in China, are responsible for patriotism, are tax officers today, and will be local businessmen after retirement. Why have to harass the lives of the people and do things that are not in line with the interests of the people. The city of Shanghai does not have any problems. In case it is affected by the sales area, all the houses will be destroyed. The merchants followed the orders. Because of the government's advocacy of domestic products, a special permanent tax exemption has been made. The above is the faith of the country and the people's livelihood. It seems that silence has been made. At the time of planting rice, the ministry sent personnel to express condolences. This is for the reason that the departments concerned have considered the idea of collecting money. The tax collection movement in Fujian Province has the suggestion of changing the phase of yuan money, which is to request that the government department of the ministry of finance and industry immediately put an end to it in order to create a broad-minded society. The above is respectfully presented to the Administrative Council of the Ministry of Finance, the Kuomintang National Government and the Department of Industry, and the Shanghai Native Cloth Industry Association.

Two Groups from Anhui Sent a Letter to President Yu 116

▲Opposing the Rice Tax The Anhui Association of Shanghai and the Anhui Society opposed the rice tax and sent a letter to Yu, President of the Supervisory Yuan, saying: [Respected President], Since the [Anhui] province has experienced changes over the years, in addition to the damage caused by bandits, the province has also suffered from floods. The province's coffers are exhausted. The people's suffering is difficult to describe. It is fortunate that the Western Anhui Red Bandits were gradually suppressed. The lives of the people of the survivors were slightly revived. Unexpectedly, the provincial government disregards the people's lives, and under the pretext of managing food, it has unilaterally restored the rice tax that was introduced by Chen Tiaoyuan and was ordered by the Central Government to be abolished. Twenty-four checkpoints have been set up in Anqing, Wuhu, Bengbu, Dashengguan, and other ports. It is stipulated that the tax for transporting rice by sailboat is 4 jiao per stone, 6 jiao for wheel transport, and 3 jiao for miscellaneous grains. The amount of tax is several times higher than the Jin. According to the total calculation, the direct loss to the people of the whole province should reach more than 10 million. How can the people of Anhui bear this? Moreover, rice is the main export of Anhui province. The average annual export is more than 10 million stones. The rural economy depends on this, and the province's financial situation is regulated by this. This year's harvest is plentiful, and the value of rice is falling sharply due to oversupply. Bankruptcies are unbearable. Now, the government is building barriers and imposing heavy taxes. The outlet for rice will be completely blocked, directly promoting the collapse of the rural economy and indirectly increasing the panic of the industrial and commercial sectors. The harm is extremely serious and difficult to estimate. Since the central government downsized the army, it has clearly announced that all similar Jin agencies are not allowed to be established. The whole country is under the banner of the Kuomintang, and there is no room for the existence of Jin under disguise. In order to uphold the prestige of the Central Government, respect the party and state discipline, and maintain the interests of their fellow villagers, the Association is unable to recognize the illegal and harmful rice tax levied by the provincial government. In addition to submitting petitions to various departments of the Central Government, we have prepared a letter and sent representatives Hu Peiru and Ke Nan to submit it. The letter requests that [you] protect the people's livelihood and uphold justice. When Chen Tiaoyuan, the former chairman of Anhui, created the rice tax, [you] submitted an impeachment to the court. The Central Government then ordered the abolition of the tax, and the people of Anhui were deeply grateful. Now the provincial government of Anhui is re-opening the old case without authorization, in contempt of the Central Government and in violation of laws and regulations. Compared with Chen Tiaoyuan, their crimes are several times greater. We dare to ask [you] to sympathize with the people's difficulties and severely impeach them in order to eliminate the wicked and maintain discipline. We also request that representatives Hu and Lei be received and instructed. [We are] anxious and waiting for orders. [Sincerely], The Anhui Association of Shanghai and the Anhui Society.

A Scene of a Love Tragedy

Li Minghui Testifies in Court 118

Audience... not enthusiastic. Judge instructs Li... [No need to appear in court next time] ▲ Did Zheng Guoyou have the power to kill Feng Deqian? ▲ The chauffeur then participated in the conspiracy. Wang Nengxiang's photo sent to Hong Kong for the convicts to identify. The notorious young lady Li Minghui's love tragedy, which was staged in Hong Kong this spring, caused a sensation. Her fiancé, Feng Deqian, died on the spot, while her lagging lover, Zheng Guoyou, was sentenced to death by the British judge in Hong Kong for inciting murder and is still appealing. As for the young lady, she returned to Shanghai after the Hong Kong case was decided and now resides at No. 8, Nanyang Road, West District, Public Concession. However, the actual murderer of Feng, Wang Nengxiang from Tongzhou, fled from Hong Kong to Shanghai the day after the murder and hid at No. 72, Xiexu Branch Road, Nanshi. After being apprehended by Chief Detective Lu Liankui, Deputy Detective Liu Shaokui, etc., Hong Kong officials heard the news and sent personnel to Shanghai to request extradition to the First Special District. The local court of the First Special District, considering that although the case occurred in Hong Kong, Wang Nengxiang is Chinese and thus should not be handed over to British officials for trial, ordered the police to detain Wang for investigation and prosecution. It has been several months since then. All the evidence has been obtained by the police from the British authorities in Hong Kong, and the only crucial witness, Li Minghui, has returned to Shanghai from Hong Kong. Therefore, Qian Hongye, the Chief of the Criminal Division of the First Special Court, scheduled a public trial at the First Tribunal at 2:00 PM yesterday, issuing a summons ordering Li Minghui to appear in court to testify. However, because few people knew about it, the audience was not enthusiastic. The trial commenced as follows: Li Minghui arrived at the court at 2:10 PM, accompanied by West Detective Huier, in car No. 3641. She entered the court and sat on the witness stand. Li's complexion was radiant, and her hair gleamed. She wore a fashionable cheongsam covered with a black woolen coat and brown silk stockings with brown leather shoes. Three gorgeously dressed young ladies were sitting opposite her, and Li nodded to them frequently, presumably they were her girlfriends. At 2:30 PM, Judge Qian and the court clerk ascended the bench and ordered Wang Nengxiang to be brought to the court. After questioning his age and origin, the police lawyer Ru Bao'yi stood up and described the occurrence of the case and the process of the investigation, stating that the case was being prosecuted against the defendant in accordance with Article 282, Clause 1 of the Criminal Law. Although the location of the incident was in Hong Kong, the defendant was arrested in Shanghai and is Chinese, so it was decided to prosecute in your esteemed court.

Feng Deqian, on the afternoon of March 24th at 8:30 PM, accompanied by Li Minghui, was passing through the Sanguang Road area in Hong Kong. The defendant and Ah Guan, who is still at large, each holding a pistol, waited there and shot Feng in the back. Feng fell to the ground in response to the gunshot, and the murderer fled the scene. The Hong Kong police immediately sent Feng to the hospital and began an investigation. Later, a live ammunition pistol was found at the entrance of No. 5, Wansongfang. It was determined that the wound Feng received was indeed caused by this gun. The next day, an examination of Feng's remains revealed that he had been fatally shot in the heart and lungs. However, the reason for his murder was still unknown at this time. The investigation continued until April 4th when

Zheng Guoyou was suspected of inciting the murder. Zheng was detained, and on the 20th, the chauffeur Xu Yongzhen was also arrested, and a pistol with three rounds of live ammunition was found in Xu's home. According to Xu's confession, the pistol found in his home was the one wielded by Ah Guan. At this point, it was proven that the gun found at the entrance of No. 5 was the one wielded by Wang Nengxiang. Xu was interrogated by Hong Kong officials on June 27th, 28th, and 29th, and he confessed in great detail. From the study of these confessions, it was learned that Zheng Guoyou had a feud with Feng. Zheng initially wanted to kill Feng but did not have the power to do so, so he conspired with the chauffeur Xu Yongzhen, and Zheng's chauffeur Liu Aqing also participated in the conspiracy. Zheng then asked Liu to find someone to commit the murder. Liu found Wang Nengxiang, Ah Guan, and Dong, etc. Currently, except for Zheng, who has been sentenced, Xu and Liu have also been detained by Hong Kong officials. Before the murder, Liu Aqing devised a way for Wang Nengxiang and others to identify Feng Deqian. Then Dong handed a pistol to Wang Nengxiang, and Xu Yongzhen also handed a gun to Ah Guan and rented a room at No. 17, Wansongfang Clothing Store as a base. On the nights of March 17th and 18th, at 7:00 PM, Wang Nengxiang waited on Sanguang Road. However, Feng drove by in a car, and Wang did not have a chance to shoot. The night before, Ah Guan was added, and each of them carried a pistol to the same location. When Feng and Li arrived, Wang fired a shot at Feng and fled to the entrance of No. 5, Wansongfang, abandoning the gun and returning empty-handed. Ah Guan did not fire, so he still carried the gun back and initially hid it at No. 17, and then Xu took it home. The gun is still in Hong Kong. Wang's gun and the confessions of each person have all been retrieved to Shanghai. After they achieved their murder goal, they vacated the house at No. 17 the next day. The Hong Kong police then learned that the house was a base for criminals and began their investigation from there, and the defendants were arrested one by one. Now, for

the sake of caution, the police have sent Wang Nengxiang's photo to Hong Kong for the convicts in Hong Kong to identify whether this Wang Nengxiang is the Wang Nengxiang they confessed to. No reply has been received yet. If the defendant is indeed the Wang Nengxiang confessed by the Hong Kong convicts, then this case is undoubtedly true and the crime is deserved. After the statement, Judge Qian summoned Li Minghui to the court to inquire about the circumstances of the incident and the Hong Kong officials' trial of the defendants. After Li gave a brief reply, Judge Qian questioned the defendant Wang Nengxiang. However, Wang claimed that he did not know anything, no matter what he was asked in court. Judge Qian then instructed, "Your photo has now been sent to Hong Kong. If the convicts in Hong Kong do not know you, then your claim of ignorance may be excusable. Otherwise, it will be difficult for you to deny it. Therefore, I will now postpone the case until I receive a reply from Hong Kong before conducting another trial." After the instruction, the court adjourned, and the defendant was taken back to the police station for detention. Li Minghui also drove away. Before leaving, the court instructed her that there was no need to appear in court next time.

How Can a Child Be Born in Eight Months? 120

丨Wang Ruying Has No Answer丨 (Grandson Is Already Four Years Old) Asking for Marriage... It's a Joke. Mao Lianqing Accused of [Fraud, Adultery, Medicine]

Mao Lianqing, a native of Ningbo and a former shareholder of the Mao Quantai Lumber Store on Sichuan Road, was recently sued by a Shanghai woman, Wang Ruying, through a lawyer, for fraud, adultery, abandonment, and other crimes. Judge Wu then asked that given she had relations in August of last year, how could a child be born in April of this year, which is only eight months? Wang was speechless. Mao Lianqing stated that the plaintiff was a prostitute whom he met through a pimp in early August of last year, on the ninth or tenth day, at the Datong Hotel, and had relations with her. He had been to No. 7, Datongli, Baker Road, once, but did not stay overnight. The house was not rented by him. The child born to the plaintiff is not his. He only had intercourse with her once, and it is impossible for such a coincidence to occur. Even the dates she mentioned are inconsistent. The plaintiff's claim that he repeatedly proposed to her is a joke because his grandson is already four years old. How could he propose to someone else again? However, he admitted to having a fling once while out for fun. He denied giving the wedding ring. At this point, the court ordered the start of the debate. After the lawyers for both parties debated, Judge Wu announced the end of the debate and scheduled the verdict for next Wednesday afternoon. It is reported that the plaintiff is a former prostitute from the Xiu Yunge brothel in Huileli, ranked fourth. However, she has now left this life of selling smiles in the brothel.

Shanghai

Hunting Report from the Tonglu Hunting Association 121

▲ Unfortunately, hindered by wind and rain, the gains were not much ▲ The trophy was won by Shen Tu Zhen. A group of more than ten people from the Shanghai Hunting Association took the Shanghai-Hangzhou express train at 6:50 PM on the 19th and arrived at Nanxing Station at around 11:00 PM. They were received by Shu Quanbao and Xia Weiru, two students from the Hangzhou branch of Zhejiang University, and stayed at the Tongshang Hotel. The next morning, they took the Jiangxing fast boat along the upper reaches of the Qiantang River to Zhaixi and disembarked to hunt along the way. At around 5:00 PM, they arrived at Gangjia, using the Fenggang Township Office as their camp. The next day, they hunted pheasants and rabbits in the plains for a day, preparing food for the mountain climb, to stretch their muscles. On the 22nd, they set off at dawn, crossing Huangyangling and Hongjia Village, and arrived at Shangnan Diaoyu at 3:30 PM in the afternoon. Surrounded by towering mountains and ridges, it was a natural hunting area. They stayed at the home of a hunter surnamed Wang, and pre-arranged an old hunter named Haigou as their guide. This man was over sixty years old, walked on the mountains as if on flat ground, and could identify animal tracks. The next day, they went up the mountain with dogs and guns, climbing the cliffs. At noon, they shot a large mountain goat weighing more than 300 pounds. Its head and mane covered the ground, resembling black moss. In the afternoon, it rained, so they rested. The next morning, it was still raining. In the afternoon, it cleared up slightly. The members were in high spirits and took the opportunity to enter the mountain again, capturing another roe deer weighing more than 100 pounds. As the day was short and it was getting late, they sounded the horn and returned. On the 25th, it was windy and rainy, with clouds and fog filling the valley, knowing that it would not clear up in a day or two. The members were all running out of vacation time and had no choice but to decide to return. At 8:00 AM, they braved the rain and moved forward, passing Niufengling, which was about 2,000 feet high. It took four hours to walk from the foot to the top. The sound of the stream was like thunder, the sound of the wind was like a tiger, and the clouds and fog obscured the view. The mud and water submerged their ankles. At 3:30 PM in the afternoon, they arrived at Shen'ao, the home of member Shen Tu Zhen, and stayed overnight. The next morning, they took a boat to Dongzi and returned to Zhakou, taking the 3:15 train and arriving in Shanghai at 9:30 PM on Saturday. This trip was delayed by wind and rain, resulting in only two wild animals and thirty or forty chickens and rabbits being caught. The animals have now been entrusted to the Commercial Press to be made into models and will soon be displayed at the Hongfa Company on Nanjing Road for enthusiasts to appreciate. It is also known that the trophy set by the association this time was won by Shen Tu Zhen. Various photos and detailed records will be published in the newspapers in the coming days.

Entering Matrilineal Marriage to Defraud Wealth 122

〓One Action Achieves Both Son-in-law and Wife, Combining Europe and the Roundness of Children〓▲Who Knows... Entering Matrilineal Marriage Is Just a Pretext to Defraud Wealth. Yao Yunzhang, a local from No. 10, the intersection of Jin Shenfu Road and Lafayette Road, French Concession, and his wife, Ms. Yao, because they were middle-aged and had no son, fortunately had a daughter in their middle age, named A'mei, who was of marriageable age and had a beautiful appearance, but her cross-eyedness was a flaw. Yao, with only one precious daughter, did not promise A'mei to anyone, preparing to find a son-in-law to rely on for life in the future. Cao Zishan, Qian Yousheng, and others introduced Wang Chengli, a local who worked as a chauffeur for a Westerner at No. 257, Anhe Temple Road, French Concession, who was willing to enter into matrilineal marriage with the Yao family. So, on June 10th of this year, he formally entered matrilineal marriage and changed his name to Yao Yongfa. Unexpectedly, not long after the marriage, disputes arose between the two sides, and their love broke down. Yao Yunzhang, Ms. Yao, and Yao A'mei then hired lawyer Gan Lin to file a complaint with the First Special District Court against Yao Yongfa (i.e., Wang Chengli) and seven others, including matchmakers Cao Zishan and Qian Yousheng, and introducers Lu Bianying, Tang Jingsheng, Wang Zhiwei, and Wu Ziliang, alleging collusion to enter into matrilineal marriage to defraud wealth, with attached civil suits. The complaint stated that Yao Yunzhang and Ms. Yao, being old and childless, in June of this year, through matchmakers Cao and Qian, and introducers Lu, Tang, Wang, and Wu, recruited Yao Yongfa, i.e., Wang Chengli, as their son-in-law, and matched him with their third plaintiff, A'mei, as her husband. On June 10th, he formally entered matrilineal marriage, changing his name and surname, and establishing a written agreement. On that day, they gathered guests and held a grand banquet, achieving both son-in-law and wife in one action, celebrating the double joy of the event, combining joy and the roundness of children, and hoping to start a family and continue the family line from then on. Who knew that Yao Yongfa's intention was to obtain wealth. Within a few days of entering the family, he falsely claimed to A'mei that he had a former lover who was now pregnant. If he did not abort her, he would be implicated, demanding 50 yuan for abortion fees. A'mei, unaware of his deception, privately paid him on June 23rd. Only a few days later, he claimed that although the former lover's fetus had been aborted, the roots still needed to be removed, otherwise it would eventually cause trouble, demanding more than 100 yuan for breakup fees. A'mei, still believing that the matter was real, paid him again on July 2nd. Before entering matrilineal marriage, he claimed that both of his parents were deceased and that he had no relatives. However, after A'mei paid the money, he suddenly claimed that his mother in his hometown had passed away and that he needed to repay a debt of 380 yuan on her behalf. A'mei, seeing that his desires were insatiable and unable to pay any more, finally told her parents about the situation. When Yao Yongfa was questioned, he realized that his scheme had been exposed and left on July 22nd. The plaintiffs invited the original matchmakers and introducers to reason with him, but to no avail. In this situation, it can be seen that the defendants are indeed colluding to enter matrilineal marriage in order to defraud wealth, which is a violation of Article 363, Paragraphs 1 and 2 of the Criminal Law. It is requested that they be investigated and punished according to the law, and that the defrauded 150 yuan be returned, and that 500 yuan be compensated for the expenses incurred during the matrilineal marriage. In addition, 10,000 yuan is requested for A'mei's consolation money. The court accepted the complaint and, on the previous day, ordered Chinese police officer Guo Xiangyao to summon the defendants, but they could not be found. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Zhang Junqing presided over the Ninth Criminal Tribunal for the trial. All the plaintiffs arrived. Their agent, lawyer Gan Lin, stated that since the defendants had not been summoned today, the plaintiffs would designate them for summons next time. Judge Zhang instructed that the case be adjourned for seven days to summon the defendants to court for questioning.

Two Convicts in the Murder of Husband Case Sentenced to Life Imprisonment 127

▲Tang Rongzhi and Gu Jide Appealed. Tang Rongzhi, a native of Jiangbei, lived in Shihuayao and worked as a rickshaw puller. His wife, Tang Yuan, was of a promiscuous nature and had an affair with Gu Jide, a fellow worker. Tang was weak by nature and allowed everything, so the two husbands lived in the same house, known as the big and small husbands. However, the woman was still not satisfied, so she strangled Tang Rongzhi to death and abandoned his body next to the railway on Zhongshan Road. After the court's investigation and identification, his nephew Tang Yuanli and others identified and reported the case. The woman and Gu were detained by the local court and prosecuted. After repeated inquiries and debates, Judge Yang Xingqian opened the court yesterday and announced the verdict, bringing the woman and Gu to the court and instructing them that they were both guilty of premeditated murder and should be sentenced to death. However, they were specially granted leniency and each sentenced to life imprisonment. Unexpectedly, the convicts were not satisfied with the verdict and were allowed to appeal. They were then taken back into custody.

Payment of Fine 129

Temporary Receipt Discovered ▲Weng Bingchun Suspected of Corruption ▲Three Key Witnesses Failed to Appear. Weng Bingchun, a local in his twenties, worked as a clerk in the Second Special District Local Court in Shanghai, working in the Criminal Execution Office. Before October 20th, because the receipt clerk Lu Nanping was absent due to business, Weng was transferred from the Documents Section to temporarily replace Lu. On the morning of the 24th of that month, three people went to the receipt office to find Weng to pay the fine of 500 yuan for the opium case defendant Min Zaide. Because Weng was not there, they did not meet him and went back. In the afternoon, the three people went to the receipt office again and met with Weng, paid the money, and Weng issued a receipt. While holding the receipt at the receiving clerk's office and requesting the judge to issue a release warrant, the three people who paid the money were waiting at the receipt office when the director of the receipt office discovered that the payers held a temporary receipt for 400 yuan issued by Weng Bingchun, with Weng's name stamp on it. Feng thought that since the party concerned had paid the fine and a formal receipt had been issued by the court, why was there another temporary receipt, and the amount was also different. He believed that the procedure was inconsistent and would damage the court's reputation. He immediately detained the temporary receipt. When Weng arrived, he questioned him about why he issued a temporary receipt when a formal receipt had already been issued. Weng stammered and took the receipt back, tore it up, and threw it away. Director Feng, believing that Weng had committed corruption, reported it to the court president, who dismissed Weng and transferred him to the procuratorate. After summoning the payers and witnesses to court for investigation, it was concluded that Weng had indeed committed corruption. He was ordered to post bail and was prosecuted according to the law by the same-level court. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Zhang Chaozuo and Procurator Deng Baosu specially opened the Second Criminal Tribunal for the trial. The defendant arrived with his defense lawyer. First, Feng Bangyan, the director of the receipt office, stated the circumstances of discovering the defendant issuing the temporary receipt and reporting it to the court president. Then, because the key witnesses, Min Zaide, Wang Delin, and the other three people who paid the money, did not appear, the official briefly questioned the defendant Weng Bingchun and ordered him to continue to post bail and reschedule the trial after the witnesses were summoned. Because the original guarantor requested to withdraw the guarantee, he was ordered to find a suitable guarantor, otherwise he would be detained. Then, the defense lawyer temporarily provided a guarantee that the defendant would submit a guarantee within two days. Then the court adjourned.

▲Recover the Stolen Money... Imprisonment. Bounced Check 132

Ye Chuanzong, in a state of desperation, ingested poison. Ye Chuanzong, a native of Ningbo, was 37 years old and resided at No. 60, Tongchunfang, Zhejiang Road, Six Malu, Shanghai. He also operated the Shengchang and Shenchang steel bed shops at Six Malu and Daigouqiao. Business was very good a year ago, but recently, due to the increasing number of businesses engaged in this industry, his shop's business plummeted. However, Ye still tried to revitalize it, so he still ordered goods from a certain copper workshop, signing checks for payment of 1,000 yuan. Unexpectedly, the steel workshop went to cash the check on the due date, but it was dishonored. He returned to negotiate with Ye, who knew he was in the wrong but couldn't come up with such a large sum of money at the moment. In a moment of desperation, he secretly ingested opium to commit suicide at around 1 a.m. yesterday morning. His family discovered this and rushed him to Renji Hospital for treatment. However, due to an overdose of poison, he died at 2 p.m. yesterday. The hospital reported this to the police station, which transferred the body to the mortuary for an autopsy. The court will be requested to conduct an examination this morning.

Sunken Barge Blocks Suzhou Creek 135

▲Sunken Ship Blocks Waterway - The Zi Lin Report states that yesterday (the 29th), a barge in the Suzhou Creek sank, blocking the waterway. Only very small boats could pass. The barge was carrying 24 tons of coal. Yesterday morning, it was sailing from the Huangpu River into the Suzhou Creek. When passing under the Old Gate Bridge, it touched a bridge pier while yielding to two other boats. The hull of the ship became horizontal. The tide was high and rapid, and the ship was immediately tilted by the tide, taking on water and sinking to the bottom of the river. The waterway at that location was blocked from 11:15 a.m. The authorities are currently working to salvage the ship overnight. It is expected that the sunken ship will be recovered by this morning (the 30th).

French Ship Hosts Shanghai Press for Tour 136

▲Beautifully Decorated New Ship　　▲Fares Reduced Next Year The new French postal company ship, the Aramis, arrived in Shanghai for the first time and docked at the China Merchants Bureau North Wharf last Saturday, hosting a tour for various sectors. Yesterday afternoon at 3 p.m., the ship moved to the Huangpu Wharf, and the company hosted a tour for the Shanghai press. Many people attended. The ship is one of the three new ships of the French company. The engine uses a gasoline-burning motor engine. The entire ship is 567 feet long and 69 feet 7 inches wide, with a gross tonnage of 21,550 tons and an engine horsepower of 11,600 horsepower. The entire ship is divided into five layers. The first-class cabins are extremely well decorated, and the swimming pool, tennis court, social room, and exercise room are all complete and extremely exquisite. There are 191 first-class cabins, 133 second-class cabins, 102 third-class cabins, and fourth-class cabins can accommodate 700 to 800 people. The original first-class fare from Shanghai to France was 104 pounds and 15 shillings, but starting on the first day of next year, it will be reduced to 101 pounds. The maiden voyage to France is now scheduled for December 3.

Inspection Report of the Bank of China 142

▲Fifty-seventh Inspection Report of the Shanghai Bank of China Issuance Reserve Inspection Committee The Fifty-seventh Inspection Report of the Shanghai Bank of China Issuance Reserve Inspection Committee states that the committee members and entrusted accountants, in accordance with the committee's rules, inspected the Bank of China's issuance and associated bank's use of exchange coupon reserve in Shanghai on November 27, 1932, and that the Director of the Currency Department of the Ministry of Finance joined the inspection. The results of the inspection are listed as follows: The total amount of exchange coupons issued was 10,794,7274 yuan, including 62,275,223 yuan issued by this bank, 22,530,227 yuan used by associated banks, and 23,141,824 yuan used by various banks and branches. Except for the part used by various banks and branches, which will be inspected separately according to the original method, this inspection of the main associated bank covers the following: The amount issued by this bank and used by associated banks was 84,800,5450 yuan. The amount of exchange coupon reserve in this bank and associated banks was 84,800,5450 yuan, including 58,813,740 yuan 0.13 yuan in cash reserve and 25,991,709 yuan 0.87 yuan in guarantee reserve. The above two items show that the cash reserve accounts for 60% of the total and the guarantee reserve accounts for 40% of the total, and both have been inspected and found to be accurate. In accordance with Rule 5, this is a formal report. Reader's Advisor

Origin and Brief Rules 146

We believe that in today's society, many problems are presented to each person, and many doubts are piled up in each person's mind. For these doubts and problems, they often cannot be answered by themselves, and they cannot get a public discussion opportunity.

We believe that all problems and doubts are not personal, because we know that the entire society raises problems, and there are no isolated people in human society. Since all personal activities are closely linked to a real society, naturally, all problems and doubts are caused by a society. Problems should be discussed and doubts should be answered. Everyone here has the right to raise everything they doubt to society, and at the same time, everyone has the obligation to discuss problems and solve doubts. Because it is not for you personally, or for me personally, or for him personally, but for the entire society. Therefore, this newspaper is now willing to set aside such a piece of land so that everyone has the opportunity to raise problems and doubts. If possible, this newspaper will hire some experts to find solutions to the problems for the proposers. If not, this newspaper will also put forward opinions here for public discussion.

1. Scope of the problem (1) Politics and economics (2) Law (3) Occupation (4) Marriage (5) Family (6) Education (7) Rural areas (8) Natural science (9) Medicine (10) Social problems 2. Method of sending letters (1) Write your name, gender, age, occupation (or the school and grade), place of origin, and mailing address. (If you continue to communicate, you must still write in detail.) (2) Next, propose the issues you want to discuss. The writing should be detailed and accurate so that people can easily understand the true meaning.

2. Please write "Reader's Advisor Department of the Shen Bao" on the outside of the envelope and attach a sufficient amount of return postage. 4. The printed stamp from the special edition of the "Reader's Advisor" column of this newspaper must be cut off and pasted on the upper left corner of the note. Letters without the stamp will not be answered. 3. Methods of handling received letters (1) Respect the purpose of the reader. All letters stating that they hope not to be answered in the newspaper, or that they do not want their names to be disclosed when answering, can be followed. (2) If the letter does not state how to answer, but this newspaper believes that answering one person will contribute to the reference value of the public, it will be disclosed in the newspaper. (3) If the letter states that it hopes to be answered in the newspaper, but it is limited by space, only excerpts can be disclosed; it cannot be disclosed at all: or if there are problems that require detailed research, and the answer must be delayed. Readers are asked to forgive me. However, those who cannot be answered in the newspaper will still be answered by letter.

Weather Report 147

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 3:30 p.m. yesterday stated that the Shandong coast and the Yangtze River basin are cold and cloudy, with local fog in the morning. The wind direction is uncertain. Along the coast, south of Qingdao, the wind comes from the northeast to the east. The typhoon appears to be dying out in the Xisha Islands. Also, within 24 hours before 3:00 p.m. yesterday, the highest temperature in this port was 6.37 degrees and the lowest was 2.9 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 6.31 degrees and the lowest was 3.42 degrees.

Shanghai Northeastern Refugee Relief Association 148

▲Monthly Donation Campaign▲

▲Urgent Announcement▲

The Northeast has fallen for over a year. The entire nation is silent, relying solely on righteous armies fighting valiantly, the dead lying strewn across the desolate frontiers, the living bathed in blood amidst the frozen skies. If we do not expand relief efforts and provide long-term assistance, the righteous armies will be annihilated, the Northeast will be lost, and China too will perish. Therefore, based on the principle of saving others and saving ourselves, we have jointly decided on the following monthly donation plan. (1) This monthly donation shall be limited to six months. (2) The Northeastern Refugee Relief Association in Peiping serves as the central organization for relief efforts in the Northeast, presided over by General Zhu Ziqiao. All donations received by this association will be remitted to them for distribution. (3) Operating expenses will be borne entirely by the initiators, without using any of the donated funds. (4) Donation collection agencies: 1. Major banks in the city. 2. Heng Xun, Fu Yuan, Tong Chun, Qing Cheng, Yi Da five money houses. 3. Education News

(Important News) Jinan Middle School Students' Opposition to the Joint Examination Spreads (Boycott of Classes and Petition March) Jinan, 30th. The student movement has expanded. Students boycotting classes include those from Jinan No. 1 High School, Zhengyi, Yuying, Donglu, Aimei, and Zhenhua seven middle schools. This morning, over two thousand students staged a large-scale petition to the Provincial Government. Civil Affairs Director Li Shuchun received the students on behalf of the government. The students demanded: (1) The immediate return to school of senior high school students. (2) A request to forward to the central government the dismissal of the education authorities. (3) A request for the provincial government to guarantee that no further oppression of students will occur. (4) An immediate removal of the high school gate guard Li Yun. After Han returned to Jinan, he conveyed that he would respond early one day. Following this, they proceeded to the Provincial Party Headquarters to petition Provincial Rectification Committee member Zhang Xicun, requesting him to sympathize with and assist them from the perspective of leading youth, and to explain the truth of the movement to all sectors. Zhang replied that matters concerning the education authorities were not the responsibility of the Party Headquarters and required further consideration. The Party Headquarters would, to the best of its ability, sympathize with and assist them within reason and agreed to discuss the return of high school students to school with the Provincial Government Education Department. At noon, the students returned to school, distributing manifestos along the way opposing the joint examination and the Ministry of Education's hiring of individuals to "anesthetize" youth.

Ministry of Education Concerned About Mongolian and Tibetan Elementary Reading Materials 153

▲Official Elementary Schools and Short-Term Elementary Schools ▲All Have Mongolian and Tibetan Textbooks Translated The Ministry of Education, in order to promote compulsory education and strive for universal access, previously ordered the National Compilation and Translation Bureau to compile short-term elementary school textbooks and distribute them to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities for adoption. Now, regarding Mongolian and Tibetan education, the Ministry has ordered the Compilation and Translation Bureau to compile four volumes of Mongolian short-term elementary school textbooks for Mongolian short-term elementary schools, and to compile bilingual Chinese-Hui short-term elementary school textbooks for short-term elementary schools in Xinjiang, Qinghai, Tibet, and the Hui region. This concerns short-term elementary schools. As for official elementary schools, Mongolian and Tibetan textbooks for elementary schools are said to have been compiled by the Compilation and Translation Bureau, which translated the eight volumes of ordinary elementary school Chinese textbooks originally published by the Commercial Press into Mongolian Chinese textbooks, named "Bilingual Chinese-Mongolian." From now on, elementary school Chinese textbooks for Mongolian and Tibetan elementary schools have been prepared, which is convenient for both teachers and students. It is indeed a major step in promoting Mongolian and Tibetan elementary school education.

[Boxing][Wrestling][Fencing][Bayonet] Exam (Part 1) 168

(Former Director of Training and Editing at the Jiangsu Provincial National Arts Institute) Jin Yiming

I recently learned that the Central National Arts Examination will be held next year simultaneously with the National Games. Upon examining the Central National Arts Institute's regulations, [Boxing], [Wrestling], [Fencing], and [Bayonet] are listed as the main examination subjects, along with subjects like the history of national arts. Here, I will describe the origins of these four disciplines, which may serve as a helpful reference for those studying national arts.

(1) Boxing Exam

The meaning of the two characters "[Boxing]": "Bo" means to capture, referring to grasping with the fingers. "Bo" also means to strike, referring to punching with the fist. The "Han Shu Yi Wen Zhi" (Book of Han, Treatise on Literature) records six chapters on "hand boxing," but I have not seen this book. Some say it is included in the "Si Ku Quan Shu" (Complete Library of the Four Treasuries). Zhou Lianggong of the Qing Dynasty said that "[Bai Da]" (barehanded fighting) is the same as today's "[Shou Bo]" (hand boxing), also known as "[Duan Da]" (short striking). Therefore, among the eighteen martial arts, "[Bai Da]" is the last, clearly indicating that it does not involve holding any weapons. This refers to "[Shou Bo]" and "[Bai Da]," both involving stances where punches and kicks can be used, as recorded in the Spring and Autumn Annals about Ju Ying and Lu Jiyou, who were skilled at wrestling, agreeing to dismiss soldiers on the spot (immediately), which is hand-to-hand combat. The Zuo Zhuan mentions that Duke Jing of Jin dreamed of wrestling with the ruler of Chu. Also, in the "Records of the Grand Historian," the biography of Guan Fu mentions drinking with Chang Le Wei Fu, who became drunk, and the two fought, with Fu striking.

The "[Boxing]" stipulated by the Central National Arts Institute is different from Western "[Boxing]," which uses hands but prohibits the use of legs. Being able to use both fists and feet aligns completely with "[San Da]" (free fighting), "[Fang Dui]" (sparring), "[Bai Da]," and "[Shou Bo]," except that only a glove is added to the fist. Refer to Article 4, Item 3 of the "[National Defense Regulations]," which clearly states that hitting the opponent's vital areas counts as "[scoring points]." Vital areas include: (1) [Punching] Areas: the front and left/right sides of the head, the brow ridge, the heart, and the liver. (2) [Kicking] Areas: the abdomen and the calf.

Appendix: Alternative names for [Boxing]:

One name is "[Bian]". The biography of Gan Yanshou in the "[Han Shu]" states that Yanshou was tested in "[Bian]" as a Qimen guard. Meng Kang notes that "[Bian]" means "[Shou Bo]."

Another name is mentioned in the Records of Emperor Ai of Han: "At that time, he reviewed [Archery] and [Martial Arts]." Su Lin notes that "[Shou Bo] is [Jiao Di], while [Wei Xi] is divided into [Boxing], [Archery], and [Wrestling]."

(2) Wrestling

[Wrestling] originated from [Jiao Di]. Examining the two characters "[Jiao Di]," the "Shu Yi Zhi" (Records of Strange Things) says that it means butting heads with horns. During the time of the Yellow Emperor, Chi You wore horns on his head and fought against Xuanyuan (the Yellow Emperor) by butting people with his horns, which no one could withstand. This is called "[Jiao Di]." The old music of Jizhou includes the Chi You play, where people, in pairs or groups of three, wear horns on their heads and butt each other, which is the "[Jiao Di]" play. Later, any game of winning with horns was generally called "[Jiao Di]," losing its original meaning. The "Han Ji" (Annals of the Han Dynasty) records that in the third year of Emperor Wu of the Han Dynasty, a "[Jiao Di]" performance was held to entertain foreign envoys, and people within three hundred li all admired it. This use of "[Jiao Di]" as a game of winning with horns began with wearing horns, and the name became synonymous with resisting and butting. The "Wen Wu Lin Jiu Shi" (Old Affairs of Wulin) mentions that the modern game of "[Jiao Li]" (strength competition) is called "Shuai Jiao" (wrestling). In the Song Dynasty, it was called "[Xiang Pu]" (sumo). Therefore, "[Jiao Di]" has evolved from "[Xiang Pu]" to "[Guan Jiao]" (Chinese wrestling). I believe that "[Xiang Pu]" contains the meaning of fist techniques and is different from "[Jiao Di]," which focuses solely on strength. "[Xiang Pu]" combines skills, while the "Li Ji" (Book of Rites) mentions that in the last month of winter, the emperor would order generals to practice martial arts, including [Archery], [Chariot Driving], and [Strength Competition]. Originally, it was said that Qin Er Shi (the second emperor of the Qin Dynasty) held a performance of "[Jiao Di]" and "[Actor]" games in Ganquan Palace. Later, Emperor Wu of Han favored this game, which is today's sumo. It is clear that "[Jiao Di]" existed in ancient times and was not adopted from foreign techniques.

In "[Xiang Pu]," one must use their palms for support and not necessarily grapple. In "[Shou Bo]," one must also look for opportunities to step and punch, aiming to strike the opponent's vital points, while "[Jiao Di]" involves grappling and hooking legs, with the main goal of throwing the opponent to the ground. The "History of the Five Dynasties" mentions that Li Cunxian was good at "[Jiao Di]." Records of strength competitions describe Mongolian beauty entering "[Xiang Pu]" circles, where contemporaries feared the lightness of their fists and hands. Also, Xie Jian of Yangzhou was over eight feet tall and immensely strong, rarely encountering an opponent. From then on, "[Jiao Di]" emphasized lightness, thus evolving into fist techniques and [Wrestling].

[Wrestling], formerly known as "[Shuai Jiao]," requires two participants to wear a "[Wrestling]" training garment, shaped like a short vest made of dense, coarse cloth, exposing the chest, with a belt tied in the arena, which is covered with sand. The participants pull and wrestle, with power generated from the legs and transmitted through the shoulders. Injuries are not penalized when wearing the garment in the arena. During the Ming Dynasty, "[Wrestling]" prohibited punches and kicks, focusing solely on wrestling until one falls. Chen Yuanyun traveled to Japan and taught the Japanese "[Jujutsu]." Therefore, Japanese "[Jujutsu]" also originated from our country's [Wrestling], except that "[Jujutsu]" includes lying on the ground and using legs to hook and sweep, which is slightly different from "[Wrestling]."

The Tong Jian (Comprehensive Mirror to Aid in Government) states that Liu Wu of the Tang Dynasty watched a "[Jiao Di]" performance with guests, shaking his shoulders and waving his arms to encourage the participants. Shaking shoulders and waving arms are characteristic of pulling and holding, which is the form of [Wrestling]. The Zhi Yan (Collected Sayings) quotes Zhou Qian's "Jiao Di Fu" (Ode to Jiao Di), saying "Charging forward and resisting backward, all are people of great strength; grabbing right and snatching left, all are using fist techniques," which all describe the state of [Guan Jiao] and cannot be compared to [Shou Bo] or [San Da]. There is no doubt about this.

Mongolian [Guan Jiao] Method: Every year in April, Mongolians worship the stars, and strong youths participate in [Guan Jiao] to determine the winner. The Living Buddha tests the participants for five days starting on June 15th every summer. At that time, the strongmen are selected by various lamas and sent to Kulun. The [Tu She] Living Buddha sits in the center, with lamas sitting beside him. First, a circular arc is drawn on the ground. Participants in [Guan Jiao] who step out of the circle are not selected, even if they are brave. Strongmen are not allowed to strip naked, wearing leather clothing and long leather boots. The [Guan Jiao] posture involves repeated kicking to destabilize the opponent and bring them to the ground. Touching the opponent's leg with one's own is not considered a loss, but touching the ground with the palm counts as a round. This is the general outline of Mongolian [Guan Jiao]. Manchuria and Tibet also value it, calling it "[Buku]." The Central National Arts Institute has adopted similar rules for [Wrestling]. Item 4 of the [Wrestling] regulations, "[Point Deduction]," states: (1) A full point is deducted if the opponent is thrown to the ground with their entire body. (2) A half point is deducted if the opponent is thrown to the ground without their entire body touching the ground.

New Basketball Techniques (38) (Not to be reprinted) By Claire Burcky, Translated by Zhang Guoxun and Qian Yiqin 169

The aggressive offense taught by Coach Oard (Piggy) Lamby of Purdue requires precise and timely movements, making it more important than hindering the enemy. Using this tactic, Kelley, Eddy, Wooden, and other four major players of the team achieved great success last winter. The number two player starts by passing the ball high to the number five player, who is running towards the free-throw line. The number four player cuts across the court in front of the number five player. The number three player also pretends to run towards the arc of the free-throw area but immediately reverses direction and rushes towards the basket after a few steps. After passing the ball, the number two player immediately follows and runs straight to receive the ball passed back by the number five player. This method can also be slightly modified as follows: the number five player does not need to pass the ball back to the number two player but can pass it to the number three or four player. Issued by the Department of Education.

Kindergarten and Elementary School Curriculum Standards (11) 170

Nature

I. Objectives: (1) To guide children to understand natural phenomena and develop their scientific research and experimental spirit. (2) To guide children to use nature to solve problems in human life. (3) To cultivate children's interest in appreciating and caring for nature and morality.

II. Types of Assignments: (1) Regarding natural phenomena: Children investigate, observe, identify, compare, experiment, record, publish, consult reference books, and answer questions about the climate, celestial phenomena, landforms, and biological characteristics they encounter in their environment. (2) Regarding life necessities: Children investigate, collect, observe, identify, compare, record, publish, conduct trial productions or trial plantings and animal husbandry, and consult reference books to answer questions about various necessary items related to food, clothing, housing, transportation, etc., in their daily lives.

III. Key Assignment Items for Each Grade Level

Natural Phenomena/Life Necessities

Grades 1-2

1. Reflecting on cold and warmth.

2. Observing and studying the changes in the scenery of the four seasons: autumn flowers and fruits, winter dormancy of plants and animals, spring awakening of plants and animals, summer flourishing of trees, and the migration of birds such as swallows.

3. Understanding the four seasons.

4. Researching methods of preventing and eliminating mosquitoes, flies, lice, etc.

5. Researching clouds, rain, and wind.

6. Recording and studying daily weather conditions and wind direction.

7. Recording and studying temperature.

8. Regarding food: (1) Terrestrial food: (A) Observing and studying the morphology and growth of local main crops and vegetables, and conducting trial plantings. (B) Observing and studying the state and life of livestock and poultry, and conducting trial rearing. (C) Studying the relationship between rainfall, climate, and crops. (2) Aquatic food: (A) Observing and studying the state and life of fish and shrimp. (B) Researching fishing methods. (C) Observing and studying the morphology and growth of local main aquatic plants.

9. Regarding clothing: (1) Identifying silk and main silk fabrics, and studying the life cycle of silkworms. (2) Identifying cotton and cotton fabrics.

10. Identifying hemp and hemp fabrics, and conducting trial plantings of hemp and ramie. (4) Identifying wool fabrics and studying sheep. (5) Researching leather and leather animals.

11. Regarding housing: (1) Researching building materials such as bricks, tiles, lime, and wood. (2) Researching household supplies such as water, fuel, and lighting (including rulers, needles, etc.). (3) Researching the structure of dwellings: sunlight, lighting, and air.

12. Regarding transportation: (1) Researching materials used for road construction (such as stones...) and types of roads. (2) Researching types and uses of boats and vehicles. (3) Researching coal and petroleum.

13. Other: Researching ordinary recording supplies (paper, stamps, inkstones, etc.).

Weekly Time: 30 minutes

Grades 3-4

1. Studying the phenology of the four seasons (e.g., leaf shedding, research on beans, winter migration of birds, changes in spring and summer birdsong, surveys, observations, research, and records of slight changes in rain, etc.).

2. Studying the relationship between plants and sunlight (e.g., comparative studies of flowers in sunlight and shade).

3. Researching poisonous plants and animals (animals such as poisonous snakes, plants such as spider lilies, pinellia, euphorbia).

4. Observation and research on beneficial insects (such as ladybugs).

5. Studying the movement of stars at night and the sun, moon, and stars.

6. Continuing items 4 and 5 from the previous grade.

7. Researching dew, frost, ice, and clouds.

8. Recording and studying temperature, rainfall, and wind direction.

9. Regarding food: (1) Terrestrial food: (A) Continuing (A) from the previous year, plus research on main fruit trees. (B) Researching the relationship between locusts, rice borers, earthworms, and crops. (C) Researching soybeans. (D) Researching tea. (2) Aquatic food: (A) Continuing items (A) and (B) from the previous year. (B) Continuing item (C) from the previous year, plus trial cultivation. (3) Researching other edible oils, salt, and sugar.

10. Regarding clothing: (1) Researching silk and dyes, raising silkworms, and trial planting mulberry trees. (2) Researching cotton fabrics and trial planting cotton. (3) Researching the bleaching effect of silk. (4) Continuing research on wool fabrics. (5) Continuing research on leather goods.

11. Regarding housing: (1) Building materials: Researching granite, sandstone, limestone, pine, cedar, and glass. (2) Household supplies: Researching common lumber furniture, iron furniture, common tools, and fire prevention equipment.

12. Regarding transportation: (1) Continuing from the previous year (2) researching ships, carts, and steam engines. (3) Researching coal and iron mining.

13. Other: (1) Researching printing equipment. (2) Researching toys: leather balls, roly-poly toys, etc., and simple physics.

Weekly Time: 120 minutes

Grades 5-6

1. Studying the causes and effects of changes in the four seasons.

2. Continuing items 2, 3, 4, 5, and 6 from the previous grade.

3. Researching earthquakes, tsunamis, and volcanic eruptions.

4. Researching the formation and changes of the Earth.

5. Studying the phenomena of the sun, moon, and Earth's movements, and the phases of the moon.

6. Studying the types and origins of stars.

7. Researching lightning and lightning protection.

8. Researching the evolution of living things.

9. Regarding food: (1) Terrestrial food: (A) Continuing items (A), (B), and (C) from the previous year. (B) Researching the relationship between manure and crops, and various types of fertilizers. (2) Aquatic food: Continuing from the previous year. (3) Researching air and the effects of air and nitrogen composition and vacuum. (4) Researching other relationships between salt, sugar, wine, sauces, soy sauce, etc., and food.

10. Regarding clothing: (1) Continuing from the previous year, plus researching clothing (2) and accessories, as well as man-made silk, man-made leather, and machine (345) manufacturing.

11. Regarding housing: (1) Building materials: Continuing from the previous year, plus researching cement, mortar, and afforestation. (2) Household supplies: Continuing from the previous year, plus researching porcelain, pottery, hardware, common tools, telephones, electric lights, stoves, tap water, and physicochemical effects.

12. Regarding transportation: (1) Researching the center of gravity of bridges and other structures and the physical effects of structures. (2) Researching the manufacture and movement principles of airplanes, bicycles, trains, and trams. (3) Researching the principles of wired and wireless telegraph equipment. (4) Researching the mining of oil and coal.

13. Other: (1) Continuing item (1) from the previous year. (2) Researching toys and recreational equipment: phonographs, cameras. (3) Researching matches and weapons.

Notes: (1) The above key items are arranged according to the classification method and separated by dotted lines. (2) The content of the key items is extremely flexible. During teaching, the scope of research should be expanded according to the children's learning ability and local conditions, and the content of the key items should be reduced, increased, or decreased at any time. If necessary, the assignments of the previous year can be continued in the following year. For example, water is only included in the first year, but when studying steam in the second year, water power should be utilized, and the scope of research should be continuously expanded. (3) The order of research should be based on the children's experience, and not strictly adhere to the order listed in the key items.

Regarding the trend of various bond prices, the market was very active in buying at the opening in the morning. Demand far exceeded supply, and prices uniformly rose sharply, continuing the trend from the beginning of the week. The strength of the rise was quite astonishing, almost unprecedented in recent years. Even the extremely weak and sparsely traded "96 Public Bond" suddenly saw someone buying, and in the late market, it soared to over 7 yuan, jumping up by several jiao (tenths of a yuan), already resembling the price at the beginning of the year. As a result, both the near-term and far-term contracts were higher than before the settlement date. For example, the whole "6" far-term and "20" customs spot goods both rose by two yuan and three jiao. The "20" roll finance December futures each rose by one yuan and eighty-nine jiao. Other bonds each rose by one yuan to one yuan and forty-five jiao. It is said that the steady and sharp rise in bond prices is partly due to the prevailing environment, and the increasing amount of silver dollars in the financial sector, due to the narrowing ratio between silver dollars and gold, is gradually being used for investment, boosting buyer sentiment. The spot goods totaled only 4,000 yuan, while the futures market reached 5.55 million yuan, totaling 14.84 million yuan.

Yarn and Cotton 178

Extremely Pessimistic Yarn Market 179

The cotton yarn market is extremely sluggish due to excessively weak actual demand and a deteriorating environment. As a result, the stock of goods at various factories is gradually increasing. With the end of the year approaching rapidly, it is becoming increasingly difficult to ease the credit situation. Therefore, the market atmosphere is very pessimistic. Fortunately, the underlying base is small and can still provide temporary support. It is said that there are more than 30,000 bales of yarn in the port of Hankou and also inventory in Tianjin, so the yarn market is particularly unstable under these circumstances.

(Benchmark down one or two taels) The market opened firmer due to rising American cotton prices, and sentiment was slightly better. The prices for each month remained unchanged for the first two or three rounds of trading, then weakened, with prices for each month falling by one, two, or three qian (hundredths of a tael). In the afternoon, news of weak actual demand caused the market to loosen again, and some manufacturers sold short, further weakening the market, with prices for each month falling by two, three, four, five, or six qian. The total daily transaction volume was 30,600 dan (a unit of weight). Longfeng sold 2,600 bales, Dafu 1,050 bales, Dafeng 800 bales, Rongxing 800 bales, and Tongxing 1,250 bales. Yicheng bought 1,700 bales, Zanfeng 800 bales, and Yukang 800 bales. The closing prices are listed below.

Cotton Market Situation Still Favorable 180

The cotton market was weak in the morning and afternoon, but the overall situation was still favorable. Due to rising American cotton prices and high gold prices, sentiment was still good, and there were still many buyers. However, with the yarn market declining daily, factories are unwilling to purchase raw materials. Furthermore, the price of Indian cotton is gradually approaching. It is said that there are approximately 80,000 to 90,000 bales of cotton in Hankou's inventory, and the supply from various producing areas has slightly loosened. Therefore, some bulls have released their positions to close out their profits. The overall situation of the cotton market is also relatively flat. (Zheng Benchmark Slightly Lively) The market opened firmer due to rising American cotton prices, and sentiment was slightly tighter. The prices for each month rose by one qian. The second and third rounds of trading weakened, and as a result, the prices for each month rose by one qian. In the afternoon, the prices for each month fell by five fen (hundredths of a qian). The total daily transaction volume was 52,000 dan. Tongfu sold 2,800 dan, Taixing 1,900 dan, Yichang 2,400 dan, Yuchang 2,400 dan, and Rongxing 1,500 dan. Jifeng bought 7,300 dan, Deji 2,900 dan, Senkang 2,400 dan, and Yuanda 1,900 dan. The closing prices are listed below.
